# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Audit Log Middleware and Backend

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement API server audit logging: the audit event creation from requests, the audit policy evaluation, the audit backend dispatch (log file vs webhook), and the audit truncation for large request/response bodies.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

I've successfully completed the analysis of the Kubernetes API server audit logging system. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've identified **22 Go source files** in `kubernetes/kubernetes` that implement the complete audit logging pipeline:

### Key Components:

**1. Audit Initialization & Middleware:**
- `audit_init.go` - Initializes audit context and generates unique audit IDs
- `audit.go` - Main HTTP middleware that coordinates the entire audit lifecycle
- `authn_audit.go` - Specialized middleware for failed authentication attempts

**2. Audit Event Creation:**
- `context.go` - Manages AuditContext and event state throughout request lifecycle
- `request.go` - Logs request metadata, objects, and response data into audit events

**3. Policy Evaluation:**
- `policy/checker.go` - Evaluates audit policy rules and matches requests
- `policy/reader.go` - Loads and parses audit policy configuration files
- `policy/util.go` - Policy utility functions

**4. Backend Dispatch (Log vs Webhook):**
- `log/backend.go` - Writes events to files (JSON or legacy format)
- `webhook/webhook.go` - Sends events to external HTTP endpoints with retry logic
- `union.go` - Dispatcher that chains multiple backends together
- `buffered/buffered.go` - Batches events with rate limiting
- `truncate/truncate.go` - **Truncates large request/response bodies** while preserving metadata

**5. Supporting Infrastructure:**
- `types.go` - Sink and Backend interfaces
- `evaluator.go` - PolicyRuleEvaluator interface
- `server/options/audit.go` - Orchestrates all audit configuration
- `admission/audit.go` - Hooks for admission controller audit annotations

packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. Here's the complete flow:\\n\\n## Audit Initialization\\n- **WithAuditInit** (audit_init.go): Creates the audit context and generates a unique audit ID for each request. Sets the Audit-ID response header.\\n\\n## Audit Event Creation and Request Logging\\n- **WithAudit** (audit.go): Main HTTP middleware that decorates the request/response lifecycle. Evaluates the audit policy, creates audit events, and sends them through stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete, Panic).\\n- **AuditContext** (context.go): Holds the audit event being constructed during the request. Manages the event state and processes different audit stages through the configured sink.\\n- **LogRequestMetadata** (request.go): Captures request metadata (URI, user, source IP, verb, object reference) into the audit event.\\n- **LogRequestObject** and **LogResponseObject** (request.go): Capture the actual request/response bodies when audit level is Metadata or higher.\\n\\n## Audit Policy Evaluation\\n- **PolicyRuleEvaluator** interface (evaluator.go): Defines methods for evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes.\\n- **NewPolicyRuleEvaluator** (policy/checker.go): Creates a policy evaluator that matches requests against policy rules and returns RequestAuditConfig (audit level, omit stages, omit managed fields).\\n- **LoadPolicyFromFile** and **LoadPolicyFromBytes** (policy/reader.go): Load and parse the audit policy YAML/JSON configuration file.\\n\\n## Authentication Failure Audit\\n- **WithFailedAuthenticationAudit** (authn_audit.go): Specialized middleware for logging failed authentication attempts.\\n\\n## Audit Backend Dispatch and Processing\\n- **Backend** and **Sink** interfaces (types.go): Define the contract for audit event processors.\\n- **Union** (union.go): Dispatcher that sends audit events to multiple backends (e.g., both file and webhook).\\n\\n## Backend Implementations\\n- **Log Backend** (log/backend.go): Writes audit events to a file in JSON or legacy text format.\\n- **Webhook Backend** (webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to an external HTTP webhook endpoint with exponential backoff retry.\\n- **Buffered Backend** (buffered/buffered.go): Batches events before sending to a delegate backend, with rate limiting and async processing options.\\n- **Truncate Backend** (truncate/truncate.go): Wraps another backend and removes large request/response objects if events exceed size limits, keeping metadata intact.\\n\\n## Configuration and Integration\\n- **AuditOptions** (server/options/audit.go): Orchestrates the creation of all audit components, reads configuration flags, builds the policy evaluator, and chains backends together (truncate \u2192 log/webhook).\\n\\n## Admission and Response Handling\\n- **WithAudit** in admission (admission/audit.go): Captures audit annotations from admission controllers.\\n- **decorateResponseWriter** (audit.go): Intercepts response writes to capture status codes and response bodies for audit logging.\\n\\n## The Complete Request Flow\\n1. WithAuditInit initializes context with audit ID\\n2. WithAudit evaluates policy and starts RequestReceived stage\\n3. Request handlers are invoked, logging request metadata, objects, and annotations\\n4. Response is captured by decorated writer\\n5. ResponseStarted and ResponseComplete stages process events\\n6. Events flow through Union \u2192 [Truncate] \u2192 [Log/Webhook backends]\\n7. Truncate backend removes large bodies if needed\\n8. Log backend writes to files, Webhook backend sends to external endpoints\\n9. Buffered wrapper adds batching, rate limiting, and async processing\"\n}\n",

contract for audit event processors.\\n- **Union** (union.go): Dispatcher that sends audit events to multiple backends (e.g., both file and webhook).\\n\\n## Backend Implementations\\n- **Log Backend** (log/backend.go): Writes audit events to a file in JSON or legacy text format.\\n- **Webhook Backend** (webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to an external HTTP webhook endpoint with exponential backoff retry.\\n- **Buffered Backend** (buffered/buffered.go): Batches events before sending to a delegate backend, with rate limiting and async processing options.\\n- **Truncate Backend** (truncate/truncate.go): Wraps another backend and removes large request/response objects if events exceed size limits, keeping metadata intact.\\n\\n## Configuration and Integration\\n- **AuditOptions** (server/options/audit.go): Orchestrates the creation of all audit components, reads configuration flags, builds the policy evaluator, and chains backends together (truncate \u2192 log/webhook).\\n\\n## Admission and Response Handling\\n- **WithAudit** in admission (admission/audit.go): Captures audit annotations from admission controllers.\\n- **decorateResponseWriter** (audit.go): Intercepts response writes to capture status codes and response bodies for audit logging.\\n\\n## The Complete Request Flow\\n1. WithAuditInit initializes context with audit ID\\n2. WithAudit evaluates policy and starts RequestReceived stage\\n3. Request handlers are invoked, logging request metadata, objects, and annotations\\n4. Response is captured by decorated writer\\n5. ResponseStarted and ResponseComplete stages process events\\n6. Events flow through Union \u2192 [Truncate] \u2192 [Log/Webhook backends]\\n7. Truncate backend removes large bodies if needed\\n8. Log backend writes to files, Webhook backend sends to external endpoints\\n9. Buffered wrapper adds batching, rate limiting, and async processing\"\n}\n",
